         E
         FEND Off Fentanyl Act
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H3903049128D34AA38185BFC2DAC071F5"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            3001.
            SHORT TITLES
            This division may be cited as the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">Fentanyl Eradication and Narcotics Deterrence Off Fentanyl or the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">FEND Off Fentanyl Act.
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H7F0F5F8A7A7446539E10EB646931F870"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            3002.
            SENSE OF CONGRESS
            It is the sense of Congress thatâ€”
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H9BAAC8C05204461A894DCBCE0223B9C7"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               the proliferation of fentanyl is causing an unprecedented surge in overdose deaths in the United States, fracturing families and communities, and necessitating a comprehensive policy response to combat its lethal flow and to mitigate the drugâ€™s devastating consequences;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HF37C7D0AFD8349FFA76351DA8D7B5FAC"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               the trafficking of fentanyl into the United States is a national security threat that has killed hundreds of thousands of United States citizens;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HF17EAB07E8794BBE90065377155E2569"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               transnational criminal organizations, including cartels primarily based in Mexico, are the main purveyors of fentanyl into the United States and must be held accountable;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H727B68477CDD49DDA4E68505BBD871B3"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               precursor chemicals sourced from the Peopleâ€™s Republic of China areâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H8B8630F42BB84492882126B9C0E7105F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  shipped from the Peopleâ€™s Republic of China by legitimate and illegitimate means;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H521FBB8E9C1F49A59019114FFE863790"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  transformed through various synthetic processes to produce different forms of fentanyl; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFC7AB06DAD8447FF87EDC2E410A14006"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  crucial to the production of illicit fentanyl by transnational criminal organizations, contributing to the ongoing opioid crisis;
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H694911BA89A9497DB503B9BE93F116D8"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (5)
               the United States Government must remain vigilant to address all new forms of fentanyl precursors and drugs used in combination with fentanyl, such as Xylazine, which attribute to overdose deaths of people in the United States;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H264862CD84154CFCB486F734907D0D40"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (6)
               to increase the cost of fentanyl trafficking, the United States Government should work collaboratively across agencies and should surge analytic capability to impose sanctions and other remedies with respect to transnational criminal organizations (including cartels), including foreign nationals who facilitate the trade in illicit fentanyl and its precursors from the Peopleâ€™s Republic of China; and
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HCF37508943B5401681028D5B36BC8869"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (7)
               the Department of the Treasury should focus on fentanyl trafficking and its facilitators as one of the top national security priorities for the Department.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H603EF73C0BAF49F28811965734B181BF"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            3003.
            DEFINITIONS
            In this division:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HCD3EC4501CBF4CEA89EB0F68066186C6"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Appropriate congressional committees
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">appropriate congressional committees meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H3B086C9AC97842E2954FDDA6A8782574"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HEB19BE821EEA4D77B8B5F281D01F2AB9"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  the Committee on Foreign Relations of the Senate; 
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H43967216977044C49FC8B91187C82130"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  the Committee on Financial Services of the House of Representatives; and 
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H1498C5846FE746A5A881752869AB4B7C"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (D)
                  the Committee on Foreign Affairs of the House of Representatives.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H18B58D97811C4971BB3C794A3B6412FF"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Foreign person
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">foreign personâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HCFDF3FCF9FC84E559258BCE63B19F914"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  meansâ€”
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5B2688B0F3C249CDA38872EAE0FE7985"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (i)
                     any citizen or national of a foreign country; or
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H06A8AD1956424916BB2EDA01670BB485"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (ii)
                     any entity not organized under the laws of the United States or a jurisdiction within the United States; and
                  
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H593D9B965DAA4A9D8E1C4879479E78E1"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  does not include the government of a foreign country.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HD562DA6736B7467587C1F9B46CA85F38"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               Knowingly
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">knowingly, with respect to conduct, a circumstance, or a result, means that a person has actual knowledge, or should have known, of the conduct, the circumstance, or the result.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H1BEABE771DE8427AAA6AA8CEA5739AAD"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               Trafficking
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">trafficking, with respect to fentanyl, fentanyl precursors, or other related opioids, has the meaning given the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">opioid trafficking in section 7203(8) of the Fentanyl Sanctions Act (21 U.S.C. 2302(8)).
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H2A06AD276A5E48AAA1D633355E08A976"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (5)
               Transnational criminal organization
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">transnational criminal organization includesâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HAA05BD891E0D4BD8923FD401617168AB"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  any organization designated as a significant transnational criminal organization under part 590 of title 31, Code of Federal Regulations;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFE553C62B3FA411587E88FA37FC3F1B7"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  any of the organizations known asâ€”
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H328BF0F374514E0982C386D83289E076"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (i)
                     the Sinaloa Cartel;
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HA7BCC384D86C46CCA704FE632C78E864"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (ii)
                     the Jalisco New Generation Cartel;
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HACC9460211DF4DDCB989C3E21F8963E3"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (iii)
                     the Gulf Cartel;
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0BE90DFD29024F47BF0BFD4C9516D8FD"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (iv)
                     the Los Zetas Cartel;
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H81120309896F4A1ABD2A5C009C85E29B"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (v)
                     the Juarez Cartel;
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0BBD84340E684771BA264D85337219AC"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (vi)
                     the Tijuana Cartel;
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HE0875E66868E43B8B54D9580234446CC"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (vii)
                     the Beltran-Leyva Cartel; or
                  
                  <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H12470E9EA6934B60AEB1BBD8D31F65A9"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (viii)
                     La Familia Michoacana; or
                  
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H8AA809FE29834AB491711410C9020FD3"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  any successor organization to an organization described in subparagraph (B) or as otherwise determined by the President.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HFDB84FE653774D5A87E8F1FAAAF07A9D"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (6)
               United states person
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">United States person meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H1B4F713EEBDF45B2B0C4943A54DE918C"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  a United States citizen or an alien lawfully admitted for permanent residence to the United States;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H93080B62D1BD4270B07CF09882224104"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  an entity organized under the laws of the United States or of any jurisdiction within the United States, including a foreign branch of such an entity; or
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFB2B7681CE8245BD8049ECFFD490A9EB"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  any person in the United States.
               
            
         
         <title id="H902C84C552D1481098BD8E021849C033"
                 qb-display-quote="yes"
                 style="OLC">
            I
            SANCTIONS MATTERS
            <subtitle id="H1DC08799833D41FA9DD2BE1F02AEEB7B"
                       qb-display-quote="yes"
                       style="OLC">
               A
               Sanctions in response to national emergency relating to fentanyl trafficking
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H238552FA8E2241F7A2913973CF1347BA"
                         qb-display-quote="yes"
                         section-type="subsequent-section">
                  3101.
                  FINDING; POLICY
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H7BCE7CECE37043AAAC35F48FE2A6A70B"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (a)
                     Finding
                     Congress finds that international trafficking of fentanyl, fentanyl precursors, or other related opioids constitutes an unusual and extraordinary threat to the national security, foreign policy, and economy of the United States, and is a national emergency.
                  
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H55BACC06A5CD44E8A2A75729C7CFDB9D"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (b)
                     Policy
                     It shall be the policy of the United States to apply economic and other financial sanctions to those who engage in the international trafficking of fentanyl, fentanyl precursors, or other related opioids to protect the national security, foreign policy, and economy of the United States.
                  
               
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H6EBAA897CDE147B7A0EC4F3CB28CCFA4"
                         qb-display-quote="yes"
                         section-type="subsequent-section">
                  3102.
                  USE OF NATIONAL EMERGENCY AUTHORITIES; REPORTING
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H4EF25000AA384A32A028FB7858C630D4"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (a)
                     In general
                     The President may exercise all authorities provided under sections 203 and 205 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1702 and 1704) to carry out this subtitle.
                  
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H6A2FB9DC1CCE4AEE9DCF91730E5EBA7F"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (b)
                     Report required
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H19C192D76D184E4CAE323F5FD2115876"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (1)
                        In general
                        Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, and annually thereafter, the President shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees a report on actions taken by the executive branch pursuant to this subtitle and any national emergency declared with respect to the trafficking of fentanyl and trade in other illicit drugs, includingâ€”
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H07830B848E414970AFB88E09C4900702"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (A)
                           the issuance of any new or revised regulations, policies, or guidance;
                        
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="HC9A0FC8A824543E68661BB25312B74C4"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (B)
                           the imposition of sanctions;
                        
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="HEA1D44F71D614A91AC799B562A44C75A"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (C)
                           the collection of relevant information from outside parties;
                        
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H9384C6AF24C84248ACC99255434743DE"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (D)
                           the issuance or closure of general licenses, specific licenses, and statements of licensing policy by the Office of Foreign Assets Control;
                        
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H2D4CD28AA37C480980CB6D403DAA66CB"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (E)
                           a description of any pending enforcement cases; and
                        
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H54C0DB85A9B840BFBF6B2E0C526B8C1C"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (F)
                           the implementation of mitigation procedures.
                        
                     
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H4689BB91E01F4E6ABCA21584FE0CBA2F"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (2)
                        Form of report
                        Each report required under paragraph (1) shall be submitted in unclassified form, but may include the matters required under subparagraphs (C), (D), (E), and (F) of such paragraph in a classified annex.
                     
                  
               
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H6BD04350575444AC896CFED642358B9E"
                         qb-display-quote="yes"
                         section-type="subsequent-section">
                  3103.
                  IMPOSITION OF SANCTIONS WITH RESPECT TO FENTANYL TRAFFICKING BY TRANSNATIONAL CRIMINAL ORGANIZATIONS
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H6031198AE6FF43DF9F1188FA474F3E1F"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (a)
                     In general
                     The President shall impose the sanctions described in subsection (b) with respect to any foreign person the President determinesâ€”
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H8B00E38320784E4AB2F876B5CE9D7CEA"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (1)
                        is knowingly involved in the significant trafficking of fentanyl, fentanyl precursors, or other related opioids, including such trafficking by a transnational criminal organization; or
                     
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HE3BF7299DF2C4418AE58AAFDE073B023"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (2)
                        otherwise is knowingly involved in significant activities of a transnational criminal organization relating to the trafficking of fentanyl, fentanyl precursors, or other related opioids.
                     
                  
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="HF5DE0EBD3A4D40E7A35EB4966BC42FD3"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (b)
                     Sanctions described
                     The President, pursuant to the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1701 et seq.), may block and prohibit all transactions in property and interests in property of a foreign person described in subsection (a) if such property and interests in property are in the United States, come within the United States, or are or come within the possession or control of a United States person.
                  
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H93A41B7EDA72444095AA1DD92B93C377"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (c)
                     Report required
                     Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, and annually thereafter, the President shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees a report on actions taken by the executive branch with respect to the foreign persons identified under subsection (a).
                  
               
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H7D4CE5C3C9E7406C93313EE7E7ED6A36"
                         qb-display-quote="yes"
                         section-type="subsequent-section">
                  3104.
                  PENALTIES; WAIVERS; EXCEPTIONS
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="HDA1BA8DFAF1A4A8FB91D3B30294D02F1"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (a)
                     Penalties
                     Any person that violates, attempts to violate, conspires to violate, or causes a violation of this subtitle or any regulation, license, or order issued to carry out this subtitle shall be subject to the penalties set forth in subsections (b) and (c) of section 206 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1705) to the same extent as a person that commits an unlawful act described in subsection (a) of that section.
                  
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H0377F653295342BA81766711CBDA188A"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (b)
                     National security waiver
                     The President may waive the application of sanctions under this subtitle with respect to a foreign person if the President determines that such waiver is in the national security interest of the United States.
                  
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="HAC0CE5F607C5454BBB88038EC8009EB4"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (c)
                     Exceptions
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H750BB1B43D864E7493A1CBD2B53CE3E2"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (1)
                        Exception for intelligence activities
                        This subtitle shall not apply with respect to activities subject to the reporting requirements under title V of the National Security Act of 1947 (50 U.S.C. 3091 et seq.) or any authorized intelligence activities of the United States.
                     
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HBC2F628C637C459FA6A5001B04B2004A"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (2)
                        Exception for compliance with international obligations and law enforcement activities
                        Sanctions under this subtitle shall not apply with respect to an alien if admitting or paroling the alien into the United States is necessaryâ€”
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="HE86719B5F5BC4DED8DD0EA42EA0EDA5B"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (A)
                           to permit the United States to comply with the Agreement regarding the Headquarters of the United Nations, signed at Lake Success on June 26, 1947, and entered into force November 21, 1947, between the United Nations and the United States, or other applicable international obligations of the United States; or
                        
                        <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="HA2B4C0EBD9A44D5799677DC63F559C0A"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (B)
                           to carry out or assist law enforcement activity of the United States.
                        
                     
                     <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H8EAC8E3EA1E7454582F405C599726A85"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (3)
                        Humanitarian exemption
                        The President may not impose sanctions under this subtitle with respect to any person for conducting or facilitating a transaction for the sale of agricultural commodities, food, medicine, or medical devices or for the provision of humanitarian assistance.
                     
                  
               
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H07B5D813A2F94771858ECEBCBE0F76BE"

                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"

                                       id="H60FBF94833A74E429925D94A6B73BE0B"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">

                  3111.
                  TEN-YEAR STATUTE OF LIMITATIONS FOR VIOLATIONS OF SANCTIONS
                  <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="H5F9BDD8478654BE7BDB7AE7DBA0FBD8A"
                               qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (a)
                     International Emergency Economic Powers Act
                     Section 206 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1705) is amended by adding at the end the following:
                     <quoted-block display-end-quotes="yes"
                                    display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    display-quotes="yes"
                                    id="HE7DBBF407AC64BF88C07FBE68B84042A"
                                    style="OLC">
                        <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                     id="H85042BD680A34D9EB4E10B49A0BAF166"
                                     qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (d)
                           Statute of limitations
                           <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H0C55B04240FE411DAB30A0C9E3EA1596"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                              (1)
                              Time for commencing proceedings
                              <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                             id="HBAEC7A47F9E94DC690DAC21B83A0E7EA"
                                             qb-display-quote="yes">
                                 (A)
                                 In general
                                 An action, suit, or proceeding for the enforcement of any civil fine, penalty, or forfeiture, pecuniary or otherwise, under this section shall not be entertained unless commenced within 10 years after the latest date of the violation upon which the civil fine, penalty, or forfeiture is based.
                              
                              <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                             id="H812496FC74854578AE025FA9684EE592"
                                             qb-display-quote="yes">
                                 (B)
                                 Commencement
                                 For purposes of this paragraph, the commencement of an action, suit, or proceeding includes the issuance of a pre-penalty notice or finding of violation.
                              
                           
                           <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H908D99AD232645EEA5AC0BC4AEEE4E25"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                              (2)
                              Time for indictment
                              No person shall be prosecuted, tried, or punished for any offense under subsection (c) unless the indictment is found or the information is instituted within 10 years after the latest date of the violation upon which the indictment or information is based.
                           
                        
                        .

                  3112.
                  CLASSIFIED REPORT AND BRIEFING ON STAFFING OF OFFICE OF FOREIGN ASSETS CONTROL
                  Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the Director of the Office of Foreign Assets Control shall provide to the appropriate congressional committees a classified report and briefing on the staffing of the Office of Foreign Assets Control, disaggregated by staffing dedicated to each sanctions program and each country or issue.
               
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HD9066131CE0D43B6A4909551B0A820B1"
                         qb-display-quote="yes"
                         section-type="subsequent-section">
                  3113.
                  REPORT ON DRUG TRANSPORTATION ROUTES AND USE OF VESSELS WITH MISLABELED CARGO
                  Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the Secretary of the Treasury, in conjunction with the heads of other relevant Federal agencies, shall provide to the appropriate congressional committees a classified report and briefing on efforts to target drug transportation routes and modalities, including an assessment of the prevalence of false cargo labeling and shipment of precursor chemicals without accurate tracking of the customers purchasing the chemicals.
               
               <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H8D22A90C89CF4563BE69B102671E7FF8"
                         qb-display-quote="yes"
                         section-type="subsequent-section">
                  3114.
                  REPORT ON ACTIONS OF PEOPLEâ€™S REPUBLIC OF CHINA WITH RESPECT TO PERSONS INVOLVED IN FENTANYL SUPPLY CHAIN
                  Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the Secretary of the Treasury, in conjunction with the heads of other relevant Federal agencies, shall provide to the appropriate congressional committees a classified report and briefing on actions taken by the Government of the Peopleâ€™s Republic of China with respect to persons involved in the shipment of fentanyl, fentanyl analogues, fentanyl precursors, precursors for fentanyl analogues, and equipment for the manufacturing of fentanyl and fentanyl-laced counterfeit pills.

               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"

                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (a)
                  In general
                  Subtitle A of the Fentanyl Sanctions Act (21 U.S.C. 2311 et seq.) is amended by inserting after section 7213 the following:
                  <quoted-block display-end-quotes="yes"
                                 display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 display-quotes="yes"
                                 id="HDBD975112AEC4CFDA55C21B463584667"
                                 style="OLC">
                     <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                               id="HED7DD716950E4A1E9069101FC6E4E800"
                               qb-display-quote="yes"
                               section-type="subsequent-section">
                        7213A.
                        DESIGNATION OF TRANSACTIONS OF SANCTIONED PERSONS AS OF PRIMARY MONEY LAUNDERING CONCERN
                        <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                     id="H25893C552C574113B9068352246C782E"
                                     qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (a)
                           In general
                           If the Secretary of the Treasury determines that reasonable grounds exist for concluding that 1 or more financial institutions operating outside of the United States, 1 or more classes of transactions within, or involving, a jurisdiction outside of the United States, or 1 or more types of accounts within, or involving, a jurisdiction outside of the United States, is of primary money laundering concern in connection with illicit opioid trafficking, the Secretary of the Treasury may, by order, regulation, or otherwise as permitted by lawâ€”
                           <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="HD22E7043BE394ED8B6C76084E87CE15C"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                              (1)
                              require domestic financial institutions and domestic financial agencies to take 1 or more of the special measures provided for in section 9714(a)(1) of the National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2021 (Public Law 116â€“283; 31 U.S.C. 5318A note); or
                           
                           <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H87061A008EAE4EE48DEBD774891D96FD"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                              (2)
                              prohibit, or impose conditions upon, certain transmittals of funds (to be defined by the Secretary) by any domestic financial institution or domestic financial agency, if such transmittal of funds involves any such institution, class of transaction, or type of accounts.
                           
                        
                        <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                     id="HB86CBD659A5E47C6A64D4C036146F9E1"
                                     qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (b)
                           Classified information
                           In any judicial review of a finding of the existence of a primary money laundering concern, or of the requirement for 1 or more special measures with respect to a primary money laundering concern made under this section, if the designation or imposition, or both, were based on classified information (as defined in section 1(a) of the Classified Information Procedures Act (18 U.S.C. App.)), such information may be submitted by the Secretary to the reviewing court ex parte and in camera. This subsection does not confer or imply any right to judicial review of any finding made or any requirement imposed under this section.
                        
                        <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                     id="H72EDFBA0F05C441BA6F82CD7D1A138F6"
                                     qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (c)
                           Availability of information
                           The exemptions from, and prohibitions on, search and disclosure referred to in section 9714(c) of the National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2021 (Public Law 116â€“283; 31 U.S.C. 5318A note) shall apply to any report or record of report filed pursuant to a requirement imposed under subsection (a). For purposes of section 552 of title 5, United States Code, this subsection shall be considered a statute described in subsection (b)(3)(B) of such section.
                        
                        <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                     id="H52B1582A9D4A48869F4C42F804567DD1"
                                     qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (d)
                           Penalties
                           The penalties referred to in section 9714(d) of the National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2021 (Public Law 116â€“283; 31 U.S.C. 5318A note) shall apply to violations of any order, regulation, special measure, or other requirement imposed under subsection (a), in the same manner and to the same extent as described in such section 9714(d).
                        
                        <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                     id="H13255A3A275B4CE890CCB16BA51A8A9D"
                                     qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (e)
                           Injunctions
                           The Secretary of the Treasury may bring a civil action to enjoin a violation of any order, regulation, special measure, or other requirement imposed under subsection (a) in the same manner and to the same extent as described in section 9714(e) of the National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2021 (Public Law 116â€“283; 31 U.S.C. 5318A note).
                        
                     
                     .

         <title id="H57921FAE73D04DEFB91C344B91F4A2D9"
                 qb-display-quote="yes"
                 style="OLC">
            III
            EXCEPTION RELATING TO IMPORTATION OF GOODS
            <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                      id="H09FCF94540D141E5B1CE3E69ECBC5BDA"
                      qb-display-quote="yes"
                      section-type="subsequent-section">
               3301.
               EXCEPTION RELATING TO IMPORTATION OF GOODS
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H399E250B6617465EABDC04D8B75016CF"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (a)
                  In general
                  The authority or a requirement to block and prohibit all transactions in all property and interests in property under this division shall not include the authority or a requirement to impose sanctions on the importation of goods.
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H20880C98462547838F0704B970382442"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (b)
                  Good defined
                  In this section, the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">good means any article, natural or manmade substance, material, supply or manufactured product, including inspection and test equipment, and excluding technical data.

            <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                      id="HB6F1267827264610AFE538E1D1C2DBE0"
                      qb-display-quote="yes"
                      section-type="subsequent-section">
               2.
               DEFINITIONS
               In this division:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H124B732B512B4D15A9E2EB49E67C3ECF"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Russian aggressor state
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">Russian aggressor state meansâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H745B89867EA944BB9A5AA25EF2777659"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     the Russian Federation; and
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H94AE0F000221480DB457CC0DFB84A382"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     Belarus, if the President determines Belarus has engaged in an act of war against Ukraine related to Russiaâ€™s ongoing February 24, 2022, invasion of Ukraine.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H9342B82E8286472F849A4B3769E881CF"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Russian aggressor state sovereign asset
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">Russian aggressor state sovereign asset means any Russian sovereign assets or any funds or property of another Russian aggressor state determined by the President to be of the same sovereign character as the assets described in paragraph (7).
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HC884D35BD7DC4F8A8BC526625BDBFC47"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  Appropriate congressional committees
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">appropriate congressional committees meansâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HAA9C730808C34068A697F45D3A6C8D18"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     the Committee on Foreign Relations and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate; and
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H0BA018B51B764FBE9998A97EF99D44AA"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     the Committee on Foreign Affairs and the Committee on Financial Services of the House of Representatives.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HD4F898C7ABBD4F50914BDED943931AB8"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  Financial institution
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">financial institution means a financial institution specified in subparagraph (A), (B), (C), (D), (E), (F), (G), (H), (I), (J), (M), or (Z) of section 5312(a)(2) of title 31, United States Code.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H7EFCB06D15BF43B6BAEA2B42816A3407"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (5)
                  G7
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">G7 means the countries that are member of the informal Group of 7, including Canada, France, Germany, Italy, Japan, the United Kingdom, and the United States.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H2B2E0CC596E9474EB6887ACB23B40B2D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (6)
                  Russian sovereign asset
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">Russian sovereign asset means any of the following:
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HBE928068768A4A889B3EC5C030BBD78C"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     Funds and other property ofâ€”
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFC7DDB8CA67C4A14AF1E0A76E7091F21"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        the Central Bank of the Russian Federation;
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H9F0A243EFAB1446AA685753A2AB2F224"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        the Russian National Wealth Fund; or
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HCB8BF317E8A7443981C7DDD01CFED18B"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (iii)
                        the Ministry of Finance of the Russian Federation.
                     
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H62EF7167BA5042D38801C1819AC05C8C"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     Any other funds or other property that are owned by the Government of the Russian Federation, including by any subdivision, agency, or instrumentality of that government.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H012A653E17D2438B96C553BA545A0223"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (7)
                  United states
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">United States means the several States, the District of Columbia, the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico, the Commonwealth of the Northern Mariana Islands, American Samoa, Guam, the United States Virgin Islands, and any other territory or possession of the United States.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HCB75EEC30B5046B88BFA272A18DB34B4"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (8)
                  United states financial institution
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">United States financial institution means a financial institution organized under the laws of the United States or of any jurisdiction within the United States, including a foreign branch of such an institution.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HD59DBF0E6A0B43F6A1695161EC1712D2"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (9)
                  Seize or seizure
                  The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">seize or <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">seizure means confiscation of all right, title, and interest whatsoever in a Russian sovereign asset or a Russian aggressor state sovereign asset and vesting of the same in the United States. 
               
            
         
         <title id="H41F281409EEF4CA5B51E7E8EA7D650A1"
                 qb-display-quote="yes"
                 style="OLC">
            II
            REPURPOSING OF RUSSIAN SOVEREIGN ASSETS 
            <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                      id="HCF672F09CA3647FEB76CE322DED522BB"
                      qb-display-quote="yes"
                      section-type="subsequent-section">
               101.
               FINDINGS; SENSE OF CONGRESS
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="HC990C410E84E43F4AA59952F6E22E8EE"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (a)
                  Findings
                  Congress makes the following findings:
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H1801552FC92C447798B5E284738F5F36"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (1)
                     On February 24, 2022, the Government of the Russian Federation violated the sovereignty and territorial integrity of Ukraine by engaging in a premeditated, second illegal invasion of Ukraine.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H612D9C52FDD84DC0A9AB7839C545786F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (2)
                     The international community has condemned the illegal invasions of Ukraine by the Russian Federation, as well as the commission of the crime of aggression, war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide by officials of the Russian Federation, including through the deliberate targeting of civilians and civilian infrastructure, the forcible transfer of children, and the commission of sexual violence.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H0192B965931144ABB4E260C802501D6B"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (3)
                     The leaders of the G7 have called the Russian Federationâ€™s <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">unprovoked and completely unjustified attack on the democratic state of Ukraine a <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">serious violation of international law and a grave breach of the United Nations Charter and all commitments Russia entered in the Helsinki Final Act and the Charter of Paris and its commitments in the Budapest Memorandum.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H8074C4F091064508A04B5095C644EDFF"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (4)
                     On March 2, 2022, the United Nations General Assembly adopted Resolution ESâ€“11/1, entitled <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">Aggression against Ukraine, by a vote of 141 to 5. That resolution <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">deplore[d] in the strongest terms the aggression by the Russian Federation against Ukraine in violation of Article 2(4) of the [United Nations] Charter and demanded that the Russian Federation <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">immediately cease its use of force against Ukraine and <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">immediately, completely and unconditionally withdraw all of its military forces from the territory of Ukraine within its internationally recognized borders.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H4EA566C0852949DFB66F8AA920358C4B"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (5)
                     On March 16, 2022, the International Court of Justice issued a provisional measures order requiring the Russian Federation to <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">immediately suspend the military operations that it commenced on 24 February 2022 in the territory of Ukraine and, in this regard, observed that <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">orders on provisional measures . . . have binding effect.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HAF37C412D3844338B6300E52ADEA155F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (6)
                     On November 14, 2022, the United Nations General Assembly adopted a resolutionâ€”
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H709B215AC774420986F17964CF6CD562"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (A)
                        recognizing that the Russian Federation has committed a serious breach of the most fundamental norms of international law and its gross and systematic refusal to obey its obligations has affected the entire international community;
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HCF8B70FFECC640FAB7FE8E87B88F86DF"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (B)
                        recognizing the need for the establishment, in cooperation with Ukraine, of an international mechanism for compensation for financially assessable damages caused by the Russian Federationâ€™s internationally wrongful acts; and
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H756A806D61C84854A4A9B7BEBADA7EF7"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (C)
                        recommending <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                   quote-display-start="auto"
                                   quote-type="text">the creation . . . of an international register of damage to serve as a record . . . of evidence and claims information on damage, loss or injury to all natural and legal persons concerned, as well as the State of Ukraine, caused by internationally wrongful acts of the Russian Federation in or against Ukraine . . . ..
                     
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H69D5F91BA912454788A5CE0B7477E48C"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (7)
                     The Russian Federation bears international legal responsibility for its aggression against Ukraine and, under international law, must cease its internationally wrongful acts. Because of this breach of the prohibition on aggression under international law, the United States is legally entitled to take counter measures that are proportionate and aimed at inducing the Russian Federation to comply with its international obligations.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H9FE7EC9342724E81AEC9C9B95E5EB954"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (8)
                     Approximately $300,000,000,000 of Russian sovereign assets have been immobilized worldwide. Only a small fraction of those assets, 1 to 2 percent, or between $4,000,000,000 and $5,000,000,000, are reportedly subject to the jurisdiction of the United States.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H4E05CAC72D2140BDA6447BAFA789C145"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (9)
                     The vast majority of immobilized Russian sovereign assets, approximately $190,000,000,000, are reportedly subject to the jurisdiction of Belgium. The Government of Belgium has publicly indicated that any action by that Government regarding those assets would be predicated on support by the G7.
                  
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H47A6718830F84928B898AA962D16105B"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (b)
                  Sense of congress
                  It is the sense of Congress that, having committed an act of aggression, as recognized by the United Nations General Assembly on March 2, 2022, the Russian Federation is to be considered as an aggressor state. The extreme illegal actions taken by the Russian Federation, including an act of aggression, present a unique situation, justifying the establishment of a legal authority for the United States Government and other countries to confiscate Russian sovereign assets in their respective jurisdictions. 
               
            
            <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                      id="HFCE7BD8C18F74E45AE866C1B46AEFA7D"
                      qb-display-quote="yes"
                      section-type="subsequent-section">
               102.
               SENSE OF CONGRESS REGARDING IMPORTANCE OF THE RUSSIAN FEDERATION PROVIDING COMPENSATION TO UKRAINE
               It is the sense of Congress thatâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HC3C394F1D2D04675AE43DB76C2123E2C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  the Russian Federation bears responsibility for the financial burden of the reconstruction of Ukraine and for countless other costs associated with the illegal invasion of Ukraine by the Russian Federation that began on February 24, 2022;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5717BA78E60C4E78A70FFFBD461FDC18"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  the most effective ways to provide compensation for the damages caused by the Russian Federationâ€™s internationally wrongful acts should be assessed by an international mechanism charged with determining compensation and providing assistance to Ukraine;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HC349CDFA98C740F48536E10885386F8F"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  at least since November 2022 the Russian Federation has been on notice of its opportunity to comply with its international obligations, including to make full compensation for injury, or, by agreement with Ukraine, to authorize an international mechanism to resolve issues regarding compensation to Ukraine;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H6DB0D8585CD5482D96BA3A05612AB6E4"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  the Russian Federation can, by negotiated agreement, participate in any international process to assess the damages caused by the Russian Federationâ€™s internationally wrongful acts and make funds available to compensate for these damages, and if it fails to do so, the United States and other countries should explore all avenues for ensuring compensation to Ukraine;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H2DAD1A0F5F3A49C28EE8CE2445B2883C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (5)
                  the President should lead robust engagement on all bilateral and multilateral aspects of the response by the United States to acts by the Russian Federation that undermine the sovereignty and territorial integrity of Ukraine, including on any policy coordination and alignment regarding the repurposing or ordered transfer of Russian sovereign assets in the context of determining compensation and providing assistance to Ukraine;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HD56028FD5A264A7596BDA5DA31F0C395"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (6)
                  as part of the robust engagement on bilateral and multilateral responses to acts by the Russian Federation that undermine the sovereignty and territorial integrity of Ukraine, the President should endeavor to facilitate creation of, and United States participation in, an international mechanism regarding the repurposing or seizure of sovereign assets of the Russian Federation for the benefit of Ukraine.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H1C1BEAFF92F6408E8A9B8D4F359EA385"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (7)
                  the repurposing of Russian sovereign assets is in the national interests of the United States and consistent with United States and international law;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5B7B60BE1D1C47C680576962A6BC8F18"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (8)
                  the United States should work with international allies and partners on the repurposing of Russian sovereign assets as part of a coordinated, multilateral effort, including with G7 countries and other countries in which Russian sovereign assets are located; and
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HF454769502FC4D9497428372CCB8A96B"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (9)
                  any effort by the United States to confiscate and repurpose Russian sovereign assets should be undertaken alongside international allies and partners as part of a coordinated, multilateral effort, including with G7 countries, the European Union, Australia, and other countries in which Russian sovereign assets are located.
               
            
            <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                      id="H03307A1F50454A01B871F134B5129D76"
                      qb-display-quote="yes"
                      section-type="subsequent-section">
               103.
               PROHIBITION ON RELEASE OF BLOCKED RUSSIAN SOVEREIGN ASSETS
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="HE7ECB65F23A84F3283E55F2871FEF75F"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (a)
                  In general
                  No Russian sovereign asset that is blocked or effectively immobilized by the Department of the Treasury before the date specified in section 104(j) may be released or mobilized, except as otherwise authorized by this division, until the date on which the President certifies to the appropriate congressional committees thatâ€”
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFBCBB608AD104D0D91B1A4D9A4979D35"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (1)
                     hostilities between the Russian Federation and Ukraine have ceased; and
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HBD4308AC056A4F2E9FF547CF7A514B48"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (2)
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H75B53E2E16EA4DD5ABF2F1D277FED89B"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (A)
                        full compensation has been made to Ukraine for harms resulting from the invasion of Ukraine by the Russian Federation; or
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HD64E6C20352B4F6DAF7E66E637A910C5"
                                    indent="paragraph"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (B)
                        the Russian Federation is participating in a bona fide international mechanism that, by agreement, will discharge the obligations of the Russian Federation to compensate Ukraine for all amounts determined to be owed to Ukraine.
                     
                  
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="HAB988FCD11A44D2FBB8D1E100467E198"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (b)
                  Notification
                  Not later than 30 days before the release or mobilization of a Russian sovereign asset that is blocked or effectively immobilized by the Department of the Treasury, the President shall submit to the appropriate congressional committeesâ€”
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HA8FDBBB8F70344A4888F169119F57E99"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (1)
                     a notification of the decision to take the action that releases or mobilizes the asset; and
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFA55BF49A35C44009310F5AF1C9C45A8"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (2)
                     a justification in writing for such decision.
                  
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="HA7A5FBC5FAAB452A983C4A8C7E934EF9"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (c)
                  Joint resolution of disapproval
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H0F0B676E3B864E2A982EAFED166C5532"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (1)
                     In general
                     No Russian sovereign asset that is blocked or effectively immobilized by the Department of the Treasury may be released or mobilized if, within 30 days of receipt of the notification and justification required under subsection (b), a joint resolution is enacted into law prohibiting the proposed release or mobilization.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HDEA6FF5DCAD644F49CE3372FF353685E"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (2)
                     Expedited procedures
                     Any joint resolution described in paragraph (1) introduced in either House of Congress shall be considered in accordance with the provisions of section 601(b) of the International Security Assistance and Arms Export Control Act of 1976 (Public Law 94â€“329; 90 Stat. 765), except that any such resolution shall be subject to germane amendments. If such a joint resolution should be vetoed by the President, the time for debate in consideration of the veto message on such measure shall be limited to 20 hours in the Senate and in the House of Representatives shall be determined in accordance with the Rules of the House. 
                  
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H837F18846C5E4011B040856272F76508"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (d)
                  Cooperation on prohibition of release of certain Russian sovereign assets
                  Notwithstanding subsection (a), the President may take such actions as may be necessary to seek to obtain an agreement or arrangement to which the Government of Ukraine is party that discharges the Russian Federation from further obligations to compensate Ukraine.
               
            
            <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                      id="H4941030C7AFC4EF2AF5D5A2610882ACF"
                      qb-display-quote="yes"
                      section-type="subsequent-section">
               104.
               AUTHORITY TO ENSURE COMPENSATION TO UKRAINE USING SEIZED RUSSIAN SOVEREIGN ASSETS AND RUSSIAN AGGRESSOR STATE SOVEREIGN ASSETS
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H2D4B23DBF5C74B648184AC9990B87AD1"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (a)
                  Reporting on Russian assets
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H0956EE60A59843F590A8146C9DA195B8"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (1)
                     Notice required
                     Not later than 90 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the President shall, by means of such instructions or regulations as the President may prescribe, require any financial institution at which Russian sovereign assets are located, and that knows or should know of such assets, to provide notice of such assets, including relevant information required under section 501.603(b)(ii) of title 31, Code of Federal Regulations (or successor regulations), to the Secretary of the Treasury not later than 10 days after detection of such assets. 
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HB1D1A3E161974A49B34DE4B093787938"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (2)
                     Report required
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H8FE02529AC1846D684986C3A0D7540EA"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (A)
                        In general
                        Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, and annually thereafter for 3 years, the President shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees a report detailing the status of Russian sovereign assets with respect to which notice has been provided to the Secretary of the Treasury under paragraph (1). 
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HA0BB5A22A2FF48F8A150CE55A1104F24"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (B)
                        Form
                        The report required by subparagraph (A) shall be submitted in unclassified form, but may include a classified annex.
                     
                  
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H572946E6C07E469E813083FBE0D4EDCC"
                            qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (b)
                  Seizure or transfer of assets
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HA627FC7EB93C4240B054599D6E7C3123"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (1)
                     Seizure of Russian aggressor state sovereign assets
                     On and after the date that is 30 days after the President submits to the appropriate congressional committees the certification described in subsection (c), the President may seize, confiscate, transfer, or vest any Russian aggressor state sovereign assets, in whole or in part, and including any interest or interests in such assets, subject to the jurisdiction of the United States for the purpose of transferring those funds to the Ukraine Support Fund established under subsection (d). 
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H7220DFBF2FED4BC3AEB51D0887A9854C"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (2)
                     Vesting
                     For funds confiscated under paragraph (1), all right, title, and interest shall vest in the United States Government, provided that no use of those funds other than the use of those funds consistent with subsection (f) shall be permitted.
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HDD4FF165DEF34FEF9A508D0DF9A8BB36"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (3)
                     Liquidation and deposit
                     The President shallâ€”
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HCF5AEBF5585148739B1A8875112C5482"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (A)
                        deposit any funds seized, transferred, or confiscated under paragraph (1) into the Ukraine Support Fund established under subsection (d);
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HDE65064C74C047148DC03A2ED5A45EFD"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (B)
                        liquidate or sell any other property seized, transferred, or confiscated under paragraph (1) and deposit the funds resulting from such liquidation or sale into the Ukraine Support Fund; and
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H764A88FD025845CFBA69ABCEBAE92D25"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (C)
                        make all such funds available for the purposes described in subsection (f).
                     
                  
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HFC61D09747474A639D8034ACA451DCAD"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (4)
                     Method of seizure, transfer, or confiscation
                     The President may seize, transfer, confiscate or vest Russian aggressor state sovereign assets under paragraph (1) through instructions or licenses or in such other manner as the President determines appropriate.
                  
               
               <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                            id="H3F8448DB29C244B999F870D99C3A5B48"

                  The certification described in this subsection, with respect to Russian aggressor state sovereign assets, is a certification thatâ€”
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"

                              qb-display-quote="yes">

                  Nothing in this section may be construed to provide the President with the authority to seize, transfer, confiscate, or vest title to foreign sovereign assets that are not Russian aggressor state sovereign assets in the United States or transfer any foreign sovereign assets to any recipient for any use other than the uses described in this division.
