                     of which the operator or owner of such vessel otherwise knowingly engages in a significant transaction involving such vessel to transport, offload, or deal in significant transactions in condensate, refined, or unrefined petroleum products, or other petrochemical products originating from the Islamic Republic of Iran;
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HC74A00303D3044DD93543FE001FE2A11"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  owns or operates a vessel through which such owner knowingly conducts a ship to ship transfer involving a significant transaction of any petroleum product originating from the Islamic Republic of Iran;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HF1A3F9F7B15C4165A22AB1501F27FC69"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  owns or operates a refinery through which such owner knowingly engages in a significant transaction to process, refine, or otherwise deal in any petroleum product originating from the Islamic Republic of Iran;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H2D35E9466B204CDAA449E06F87CEEEB9"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  is a covered family member of a foreign person described in paragraph (1), (2), or (3); or
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0E5891D0E97A4D07BF20071811176249"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (5)
                  is owned or controlled by a foreign person described in paragraph (1), (2), or (3), and knowingly engages in an activity described in paragraph (1), (2), or (3).
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H3F4E2C35EA9141DD88F9B22F2B96F4CC"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (c)
               Sanctions described
               The sanctions described in this subsection with respect to a foreign person described in subsection (a) are the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H3EA83BD915D7441E9B4BCA17330C0262"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Sanctions on foreign vessels
                  Subject to such regulations as the President may prescribe, the President may prohibit a vessel described in subsection (b)(1)(A) or (b)(1)(B) from landing at any port in the United Statesâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HEF4B046E91184AD58C0B2D5CDBCC892E"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     with respect to a vessel described in subsection (b)(1)(A), for a period of not more than 2 years beginning on the date on which the President imposes sanctions with respect to a related foreign port described in subsection (b)(1)(A); and
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HFF5CDE4C015D4BF2AEE03BC8E8355823"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     with respect to a vessel described in subsection (b)(1)(B), for a period of not more than 2 years.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HCB14CAF50466487C973D6D088EA94D4D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Blocking of property
                  The President shall exercise all of the powers granted to the President under the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1701 et seq.) to the extent necessary to block and prohibit all transactions in property and interests in property of the foreign person if such property and interests in property are in the United States, come within the United States, or are or come within the possession or control of a United States person.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H6E66F96357E64EEE95709615847AA306"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  Ineligibility for visas, admission, or parole
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HFB99BE4D45064B88B7E9724C72D0806E"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     Visas, admission, or parole
                     An alien described in subsection (a) isâ€”
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H9A07B963CC344982826E162108605086"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        inadmissible to the United States;
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H33E652550DF44727A06B4D24E3D8A9ED"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        ineligible to receive a visa or other documentation to enter the United States; and
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H175019BE34214765813AA93085D64E46"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (iii)
                        otherwise ineligible to be admitted or paroled into the United States or to receive any other benefit under the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1101 et seq.).
                     
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5774B1A658F74607A2241756F61BF65F"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     Current visas revoked
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H78FD85D75398459A9CFD927C7190B9AE"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        In general
                        An alien described in subsection (a) is subject to revocation of any visa or other entry documentation regardless of when the visa or other entry documentation is or was issued.
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H1BA30392EAD64258984071386440D0F9"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        Immediate effect
                        A revocation under clause (i) shall take effect immediately and automatically cancel any other valid visa or entry documentation that is in the alienâ€™s possession.
                     
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HD2DCDA458DEA4C1FB1F751AE993A8E72"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (C)
                     Exceptions
                     Sanctions under this paragraph shall not apply with respect to an alien if admitting or paroling the alien into the United States is necessaryâ€”
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H3D7ACD8A671F41B2B863E1642BC98FA7"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        to permit the United States to comply with the Agreement regarding the Headquarters of the United Nations, signed at Lake Success June 26, 1947, and entered into force November 21, 1947, between the United Nations and the United States, or other applicable international obligations; or
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H2AA1BBFE83EC4161B5E6C2A5BD3BC10D"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        to carry out or assist law enforcement activity in the United States.
                     
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H1CCEA62909DC414890E3E0B38A23F66F"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  Penalties
                  The penalties provided for in subsections (b) and (c) of section 206 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1705) shall apply to a person that violates, attempts to violate, conspires to violate, or causes a violation of this section or any regulations promulgated to carry out this section to the same extent that such penalties apply to a person that commits an unlawful act described in section 206(a) of that Act.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HB58B36648E0044F2A804A4239DA09AA8"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (d)
               Rules of construction
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HA545729CACCE4B4E9AA1F34470C20208"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  For purposes of determinations under subsection (a) that a foreign person engaged in activities described in subsection (b), a foreign person shall not be determined to know that petroleum or petroleum products originated from Iran if such person relied on a certificate of origin or other documentation confirming that the origin of the petroleum or petroleum products was a country other than Iran, unless such person knew or had reason to know that such documentation was falsified.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HFF287F66CC7E44D1A54629693B438B43"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Nothing in this division shall be construed to affect the availability of any existing authorities to issue waivers, exceptions, exemptions, licenses, or other authorization.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H0B2421B8BB014425B30BAF3DE7D2DA9B"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (e)
               Implementation; regulations
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H7007379C8E0344B3BAB9759EFE5FF4FE"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  The President may exercise all authorities under sections 203 and 205 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1702 and 1704) for purposes of carrying out this section.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HC4E2FCB0158E4F94995B19B6DF0ED5BE"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Deadline for regulations
                  Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the President shall prescribe such regulations as may be necessary for the implementation of this division.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HB629DDFDA40D40CFBDF6CEE809BDD4BD"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  Notification to congress
                  Not later than 10 days before the prescription of regulations under paragraph (2), the President shall brief and provide written notification to the appropriate congressional committees regardingâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H53DFCC139B7E4DFC8871AA84FD2E4549"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     the proposed regulations; and
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HEB8F4F234EC443CDB490B93C98AD6C2D"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     the specific provisions of this division that the regulations are implementing.
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H8BFC6F0B38A5460380ACCD15AE3392DC"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (f)
               Exception for humanitarian assistance
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HE2AB6068BDF44A499EDEFFF2F37227B7"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  Sanctions under this section shall not apply toâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H254FFABBB24149519247FF70681D9C12"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     the conduct or facilitation of a transaction for the provision of agricultural commodities, food, medicine, medical devices, or humanitarian assistance, or for humanitarian purposes; or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HDD9A59681D424B5596FBB2401A684F1B"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     transactions that are necessary for or related to the activities described in subparagraph (A).
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HB5963078A1CF4E6B8B006B95961BFA8B"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Definitions
                  In this subsection:
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5791EAF05A5E419BAA39D3A396ED3F5B"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     Agricultural commodity
                     The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">agricultural commodity has the meaning given that term in section 102 of the Agricultural Trade Act of 1978 (7 U.S.C. 5602).
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H8CBF979B375C462BA95E277D1EE76D2B"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     Medical device
                     The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">medical device has the meaning given the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">device in section 201 of the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (21 U.S.C. 321).
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HD93DFB518BEC420197C42CCD04758721"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (C)
                     Medicine
                     The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">medicine has the meaning given the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                quote-display-start="auto"
                                quote-type="text">drug in section 201 of the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act (21 U.S.C. 321).
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H9D6AF8CE6F4F49C282379BC16BA85676"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (g)
               Exception for safety of vessels and crew
               Sanctions under this section shall not apply with respect to a person providing provisions to a vessel otherwise subject to sanctions under this section if such provisions are intended for the safety and care of the crew aboard the vessel, the protection of human life aboard the vessel, or the maintenance of the vessel to avoid any environmental or other significant damage.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HA3A3DAEFD07846D0AB1E8A70763C9E15"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (h)
               Waiver
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H3BB6FCA1CB204E5193FCBDCA62A9AD2E"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  The President may, on a case-by-case basis and for periods not to exceed 180 days each, waive the application of sanctions imposed with respect to a foreign person under this section if the President certifies to the appropriate congressional committees, not later than 15 days after such waiver is to take effect, that the waiver is vital to the national interests of the United States.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5D2BFD853AF84E9EBDDCEBF9BB8587DA"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Special rule
                  The President shall not be required to impose sanctions under this section with respect to a foreign person described in subsection (a) if the President certifies in writing to the appropriate congressional committees that the foreign personâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H669C9BD622B54516AE9105060D6D1B2D"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     is no longer engaging in activities described in subsection (b); or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H6FE438E99A964F5E913CA7389A7BFDEF"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     has taken and is continuing to take significant, verifiable steps toward permanently terminating such activities.
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HB59343378AD84E06A21780517FABD5C3"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (i)
               Termination
               The authorities provided by this section shall cease to have effect on and after the date that is 30 days after the date on which the President certifies to the appropriate congressional committees thatâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H91D8FF51C5184ACC8742D5861406F3CE"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  the Government of Iran no longer repeatedly provides support for international terrorism as determined by the Secretary of State pursuant toâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HED7B6CC1B38B4040B726666BC8B223C1"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     section 1754(c)(1)(A) of the Export Control Reform Act of 2018 (50 U.S.C. 4318(c)(1)(A));
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H802944AB794B4E43901131F44571EC47"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     section 620A of the Foreign Assistance Act of 1961 (22 U.S.C. 2371);
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H391B765B1E804BA783CC7D70B83C909C"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (C)
                     section 40 of the Arms Export Control Act (22 U.S.C. 2780); or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5290F88E91A849B6AAD92AABD8662EE5"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (D)
                     any other provision of law; and
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H040B6139059245FB9006B2458CC92DC8"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Iran has ceased the pursuit, acquisition, and development of, and verifiably dismantled, its nuclear, biological, and chemical weapons, ballistic missiles, and ballistic missile launch technology.
               
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HD1E9B7730D554F038EB93F2B55D45C0A"

            4.
            REPORT ON IRANIAN PETROLEUM AND PETROLEUM PRODUCTS EXPORTS
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H5F35C705DE304B0089F256A89C6A6386"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               Not later than 120 days after the date of enactment of this division, and annually thereafter until the date described in subsection (d), the Administrator of the Energy Information Administration shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees a report describing Iranâ€™s growing exports of petroleum and petroleum products, that includes the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"

            6.
            DEFINITIONS
            In this division:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H38F7D2DB6686455FAD31AC341E88AE5B"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Appropriate congressional committees
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">appropriate congressional committees meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H326F13331DEC4A19A016DBFEA6043559"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  the Committee on Foreign Affairs, the Committee on the Judiciary, and the Committee on Financial Services of the House of Representatives; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HF368AC64DE4F461DA9F4EA3AEFD37BB9"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  the Committee on Foreign Relations, the Committee on the Judiciary, and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H69BA672E82974F31B89C819C50835AB6"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Covered family member
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">covered family member, with respect to a foreign person who is an individual, means a spouse, adult child, parent, or sibling of the person who engages in the sanctionable activity described under section 3 or who demonstrably benefits from such activity.
            
         
      
      
         K
         Fight Crime Act 
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H9F9E328EBB224AD49928955FAE43CC7B"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            1.
            SHORT TITLE
            This division may be cited as the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">Fight and Combat Rampant Iranian Missile Exports Act or the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">Fight CRIME Act.
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H9BDEBBEFE9E2418B8752FB0443964A1F"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            2.
            FINDINGS
            Congress makes the following findings:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HC8C075F45CD64649B48675EEB983EA51"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 (2015) restricts certain missile-related activities and transfers to and from Iran, including all items, materials, equipment, goods, and technology set out in the Missile Technology Control Regime Annex, absent advance, case-by-case approval from the United Nations Security Council.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HF94169513FC949B7B5DED703756FCE8B"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Iran has transferred Shahed and Mohajer drones, covered under the Missile Technology Control Regime Annex, to the Russian Federation, the Government of Ethiopia, and other Iran-aligned entities, including the Houthis in Yemen and militia units in Iraq, without prior authorization from the United Nations Security Council, in violation of the restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HE0602B4C82174ADB8F6362EF178F65C0"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               Certain missile-related restrictions in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 expired in October 2023, removing international legal restrictions on missile-related activities and transfers to and from Iran.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H741C270E5CB54D258C110A82973E3BFC"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            3.
            STATEMENT OF POLICY
            It is the policy of the United Statesâ€”
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HF8280D92899542F09697753B6902E494"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               to urgently seek the extension of missile-related restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 (2015);
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HC6CB681BF8824CFC8CB33A895DD8D43F"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               to use all available authorities to constrain Iranâ€™s domestic ballistic missile production capabilities;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HF125260E902847CEA9F2E24388A2286B"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               to combat and deter the transfer of conventional and non-conventional arms, equipment, material, and technology to, or from Iran, or involving the Government of Iran; and
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HD1691A10094E4FC5AED5F2A1A6F113C9"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               to ensure countries, individuals, and entities engaged in, or attempting to engage in, the acquisition, facilitation, or development of arms and related components and technology subject to restrictions under Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 are held to account under United States and international law, including through the application and enforcement of sanctions and use of export controls, regardless of whether the restrictions under Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 remain in effect following their anticipated expiration in October 2023.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HA889E52066F946D0BBA02CFFBB477654"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            4.
            REPORT
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H50E42A2D899A44D195849F89BCEFD900"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               Not later than 90 days after the date of the enactment of this division, and annually thereafter for two years, the Secretary of State, in coordination with the heads of other appropriate Federal agencies, shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees an unclassified report, with a classified annex if necessary, that includes the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H73C58AA56D294462AD0ED3B49191D677"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  A diplomatic strategy to secure the renewal of international restrictions on certain missile-related activities, including transfers to and from Iran set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 (2015).
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HBE1D138863F646E4B3F78E55BE724C46"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  An analysis of how the expiration of missile-related restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 impacts the Government of Iranâ€™s arms proliferation and malign activities, including as the restrictions relate to cooperation with, and support for, Iran-aligned entities and allied countries.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H1BBF99B4761E407388B4198E1C39127D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  An assessment of the revenue, or in-kind benefits, accrued by the Government of Iran, or Iran-aligned entities, as a result of a lapse in missile-related restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H466E4D6B18304EA1AFC6CEF4378D79EE"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  A detailed description of a United States strategy to deter, prevent, and disrupt the sale, purchase, or transfer of covered technology involving Iran absent restrictions pursuant to Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HC9C256422CA6482DA51CACF338F4C19D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (5)
                  An identification of any foreign person engaging in, enabling, or otherwise facilitating any activity involving Iran restricted under Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231, regardless of whether such restrictions remain in effect after October 2023.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H37BBDAE626F64099B216DCE563E50DCF"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (6)
                  A description of actions by the United Nations and other multilateral organizations, including the European Union, to hold accountable foreign persons that have violated the restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231, and efforts to prevent further violations of such restrictions.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H417F349C1D9443449C85722D8B7E370C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (7)
                  A description of actions by individual member states of the United Nations Security Council to hold accountable foreign persons that have violated restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 and efforts to prevent further violations of such restrictions.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H98A2A46035394487A3EB61D6AFAFEDA7"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (8)
                  A description of actions by the Peopleâ€™s Republic of China, the Russian Federation, or any other country to prevent, interfere with, or undermine efforts to hold accountable foreign persons that have violated the restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231, including actions to restrict United Nations-led investigations into suspected violations of such restrictions, or limit funding to relevant United Nations offices or experts.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0CA5FE4AF6A34A56895E93F110C93671"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (9)
                  An analysis of the foreign and domestic supply chains in Iran that directly or indirectly facilitate, support, or otherwise aid the Government of Iranâ€™s drone or missile program, including storage, transportation, or flight-testing of related goods, technology, or components.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H4FB16B46316841F1BCFC5375E9EF1D14"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (10)
                  An identification of any foreign person, or network containing foreign persons, that enables, supports, or otherwise facilitates the operations or maintenance of any Iranian airline subject to United States sanctions or export control restrictions.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H64003DE07F5E414C87DDAB938E88AABD"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (11)
                  An assessment of how the continued operation of Iranian airlines subject to United States sanctions or export control restrictions impacts the Government of Iranâ€™s ability to transport or develop arms, including covered technology.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HCEF54EB38B74445A8B66EAFB14DB819D"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Scope
               The initial report required by subsection (a) shall address the period beginning on January 1, 2021, and ending on the date that is 90 days after date of the enactment of this division, and each subsequent report shall address the one-year period following the conclusion of the prior report.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H8A0881681C414F0D9E952563E2FB2E67"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            5.
            SANCTIONS TO COMBAT THE PROLIFERATION OF IRANIAN MISSILES
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H46207DD894B1493183815267DA206A14"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               The sanctions described in subsection (b) shall apply to any foreign person the President determines, on or after the date of the enactment of this divisionâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H4D5ED3EE907E43B990D02C5DCAF78A57"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  knowingly engages in any effort to acquire, possess, develop, transport, transfer, or deploy covered technology to, from, or involving the Government of Iran or Iran-aligned entities, regardless of whether the restrictions set forth in Annex B to United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 (2015) remain in effect after October 2023;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H7D046E57236144AC8B27D144689DEFDF"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  knowingly provides entities owned or controlled by the Government of Iran or Iran-aligned entities with goods, technology, parts, or components, that may contribute to the development of covered technology;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H029B6B2C49C741E99B3703D48DEFA42F"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  knowingly participates in joint missile or drone development, including development of covered technology, with the Government of Iran or Iran-aligned entities, including technical training, storage, and transport;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5D0F349234264E9B853112745B70A117"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  knowingly imports, exports, or re-exports to, into, or from Iran, whether directly or indirectly, any significant arms or related materiel prohibited under paragraph (5) or (6) to Annex B of United Nations Security Council Resolution 2231 (2015) as of April 1, 2023;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5357EBE659D74E1FBDA3CE5EC9DE417D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (5)
                  knowingly provides significant financial, material, or technological support to, or knowingly engages in a significant transaction with, a foreign person subject to sanctions for conduct described in paragraph (1), (2), (3), or (4); or
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H82978ACFCC074FD29FF5603E3FB2B993"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (6)
                  is an adult family member of a person subject to sanctions for conduct described in paragraph (1), (2), (3), or (4).
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H552757DB914D421A8EA2F6B84F687494"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Sanctions described
               The sanctions described in this subsection are the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HD9651CF7E4E449D9B6D102C9542E7362"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Blocking of property
                  The President shall exercise all authorities granted under the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1701 et seq.) to the extent necessary to block and prohibit all transactions in property and interests in property of the foreign person if such property and interests in property are in the United States, come within the United States, or come within the possession or control of a United States person.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H940DFD109BC64273BE4BCD2B7B811761"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Ineligibility for visas, admission, or parole
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HD5321E45E54F40A19C56B08586B04B4E"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     Visas, admission, or parole
                     An alien described in subsection (a) shall beâ€”
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H6518390868F84CABB081AB8C23885E46"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        inadmissible to the United States;
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HB469AEAAAFE54163AAA1D765E4A4173C"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        ineligible to receive a visa or other documentation to enter the United States; and
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H750A8F140594440497A74B47AB6522BF"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (iii)
                        otherwise ineligible to be admitted or paroled into the United States or to receive any other benefit under the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1101 et 16 seq.).
                     
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5B52B6374BEB4F46891D1B4495370817"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     Current visas revoked
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H0ECDCB845DEF492A81EA84C92AE70CA2"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        In general
                        The visa or other entry documentation of any alien described in subsection (a) is subject to revocation regardless of the issue date of the visa or other entry documentation.
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H226E2A02847D4466A8D342F88E62FF5F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        Immediate effect
                        A revocation under clause (i) shall, in accordance with section 221(i) of the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1201(i))â€”
                        <subclause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H8EB5FA186BDF4BD3914670007FE07DDA"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (I)
                           take effect immediately; and
                        
                        <subclause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="H431C8EFD6F3349C49EED546D1B7F355C"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (II)
                           cancel any other valid visa or entry documentation that is in the possession of the alien.
                        
                     
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H6D8067C789EA413E815EBC7557D44F3C"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (c)
               Penalties
               Any person that violates, or attempts to violate, subsection (b) or any regulation, license, or order issued pursuant to that subsection, shall be subject to the penalties set forth in subsections (b) and (c) of section 206 of the International Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1705) to the same extent as a person that commits an unlawful act described in subsection (a) of that section.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H227F7606A1004C4E9CA9E5AF9F9BC790"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (d)
               Waiver
               The President may waive the application of sanctions under this section with respect to a foreign person for renewable periods not to exceed 180 days only if, not later than 15 days after the date on which the waiver is to take effect, the President submits to the appropriate congressional committees a written determination and justification that the waiver is in the vital national security interests of the United States.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H992F42835B9F4E5B89C353DA2437FA08"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (e)
               Implementation
               The President may exercise all authorities provided under sections 203 and 205 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1702 and 1704) to carry out any amendments made by this section.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H2DF85AE7932C4A9E987938BB0A867C45"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (f)
               Regulations
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5A3B38337A6B4820812DC8A36480E9EF"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  The President shall, not later than 120 days after the date of the enactment of this division, promulgate regulations as necessary for the implementation of this division and the amendments made by this division.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HDB883400A4D64BCAA2F1F74A276B1E5D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Notification to congress
                  Not less than 10 days before the promulgation of regulations under subsection (a), the President shall notify the appropriate congressional committees of the proposed regulations and the provisions of this division and the amendments made by this division that the regulations are implementing.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H2895C958C1A34460B2E80FABC15A4342"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (g)
               Exceptions
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HE2AB2A15D2D34E4AA757F0D80B0E1048"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Exception for intelligence activities
                  Sanctions under this section shall not apply to any activity subject to the reporting requirements under title V of the National Security Act of 1947 (50 U.S.C. 3091 et seq.) or any authorized intelligence activities of the United States.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H6E9CD95F24CB45958D6A0CDBCB2CF49D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Exception to comply with international obligations and for law enforcement activities
                  Sanctions under this section shall not apply with respect to an alien if admitting or paroling the alien into the United States is necessaryâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H8285805EECD34DAC9679BB374D26BE22"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     to permit the United States to comply with the Agreement regarding the Headquarters of the United Nations, signed at Lake Success June 26, 1947, and entered into force November 21, 1947, between the United Nations and the United States, or other applicable international obligations; or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5704B06DBA3143A08BDE41A9C109A21D"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     to carry out or assist authorized law enforcement activity in the United States.
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H0FA5DB9958CA4CEF8D80B1528DCBA4D1"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (h)
               Termination of sanctions
               This section shall cease to be effective beginning on the date that is 30 days after the date on which the President certifies to the appropriate congressional committees thatâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H24415889A6EC4096B89BD738B7415DE3"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  the Government of Iran no longer repeatedly provides support for international terrorism as determined by the Secretary of State pursuant toâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H70C50D2DC6DB4EDE895D90D7F1C03E6E"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     section 1754(c)(1)(A) of the Export Control Reform Act of 2018 (50 U.S.C. 4318(c)(1)(A));
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H14D1AEF155534F6FB192CA4EB676E5A9"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     section 620A of the Foreign Assistance Act of 1961 (22 U.S.C. 2371);
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HA190FB2284CB44D58CBCEBEE007BFF44"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (C)
                     section 40 of the Arms Export Control Act (22 U.S.C. 2780); or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H11CC3D9C3BAD467099435BD510AFDC07"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (D)
                     any other provision of law; and
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HEC6B145671DF4319B51C6F2C45322BC8"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Iran has ceased the pursuit, acquisition, and development of, and verifiably dismantled its, nuclear, biological, and chemical weapons and ballistic missiles and ballistic missile launch technology.
               
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H093ADF9E585B47E08FB6214F8AD94F9E"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            6.
            REPORT TO IDENTIFY, AND DESIGNATION AS FOREIGN TERRORIST ORGANIZATIONS OF, IRANIAN PERSONS THAT HAVE ATTACKED UNITED STATES CITIZENS USING UNMANNED COMBAT AERIAL VEHICLES
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HE48785E1E2EA4CB9A17AE41391D67B26"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               Not later than 90 days after the date of the enactment of this division, and every 180 days thereafter, the Secretary of State shall submit to the appropriate congressional committees a report that identifies, for the period specified in subsection (b), any Iranian person that has attacked a United States citizen using an unmanned combat aerial vehicle, as defined for the purpose of the United Nations Register of Conventional Arms.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H78C13B34ADA2412BACD9F98B14A7F4CD"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Period specified
               The period specified in this subsection isâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0E94C6F9E7BD4199ABFFA85B13893A52"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  for the initial report, the periodâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HAE0A154BF11648AEBE5C079F583F0B07"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     beginning on October 27, 2023; and
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H9142DCE787EF4E98B41F4AD319AA1D2C"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     ending on the date such report is submitted; and
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H2219599270D34AE9B9E4A108F23AEE49"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  for the second or a subsequent report, the periodâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HE7857649DC8D4B98BB68D89CBEE3A489"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     beginning on the date the preceding report was submitted; and
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H86D597F6BCCC4E78A19128E65BF9FA84"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     ending on the date such second or subsequent report is submitted.
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H207527215AE7419B8918473C2DCF7004"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (c)
               Designation of persons as foreign terrorist organizations
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H25A8C2C6AB044E759D67FE35F977D648"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  The President shall designate any person identified in a report submitted under subsection (a) as a foreign terrorist organization under section 219 of the Immigration and Naturalization Act (8 U.S.C. 1189).
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H83495FAD6AA8466CBC16A355A9EBD38C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Revocation
                  The President may not revoke a designation made under paragraph (1) until the date that is 4 years after the date of such designation.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HF20C8DE5EEAF43918B00FF9A94615BA3"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (d)
               Waiver
               The Secretary of State may waive the requirements of this section upon a determination and certification to the appropriate congressional committees that such a waiver is in the vital national security interests of the United States.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H4E9317770D274D8CA92CE5208DD4B5AC"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (e)
               Sunset
               This section shall terminate on the date that is 4 years after the date of the enactment of this division.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HAE2E4B8B280C408AB8FF5E79E727080A"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (f)
               Iranian person defined
               In this section, the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Iranian personâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0400E7B29082483B985DE0E06A517867"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  means an entity organized under the laws of Iran or otherwise subject to the jurisdiction of the Government of Iran; and
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H3279E3502E184C7C97F98F6DAE4C0CF4"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  includes the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps.
               
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HF5C062FC0CAF4216BBF1055BDAAA69D8"

                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            7.
            DEFINITIONS
            In this division:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HC916C1EF915444529EFF3D7DAAF347BF"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Appropriate congressional committees
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">appropriate congressional committees meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H4973276A93E04FA1AD0856BBA0396A19"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  the Committee on Foreign Affairs, the Committee on Financial Services, and the Committee on the Judiciary of the House of Representatives; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HE93EAFE9CD954331960D6E0A468324C8"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  the Committee on Foreign Relations, the Committee on the Judiciary, and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H6DD12F87FB87415EA47DCDF8264795E1"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Foreign person
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">foreign personâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HF1C75801581949E7B3A000249541DAF4"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  means an individual or entity that is not a United States person; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HF3A748BE706444A1A1CDE720EA302FCB"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  includes a foreign state (as such term is defined in section 1603 of title 28, United States Code).
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H8BCA4837616E4A2AB1AC9950FE07BAFE"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               Government of Iran
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Government of Iran has the meaning given such term in section 560.304 of title 31, Code of Federal Regulations, as such section was in effect on January 1, 2021.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H83CEF73E111D45B1BCF531DDFC1DAB90"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               United states person
               The terms <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">United States person meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H32D07B4E841C4C269FE0682675DCAA02"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  a United States citizen;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H035ED7C5D6A84A5F8FD5D6D0F9E9B056"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  a permanent resident alien of the United States;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H400E6339D8204BDABE17660BE1FA3E29"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  an entity organized under the laws of the United States or of any jurisdiction within the United States, including a foreign branch of such an entity; or
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HDA7B1D632DAA45348DAB81294D7D5CFA"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (D)
                  a person in the United States.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H8DF9C43837D04A17BECB034D86129AF3"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (5)
               Iran-aligned entity
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Iran-aligned entity means a foreign person thatâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HC94EC2B48E974551803259F189FCA2D8"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  is controlled or significantly influenced by the Government of Iran; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H931BCE06D44942FDA98BE3AEB890B64F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  knowingly receives material or financial support from the Government of Iran, including Hezbollah, the Houthis, or any other proxy group that furthers Iranâ€™s national security objectives.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H5D85B0F77B2C4A35A0055B6162E80682"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (6)
               Covered technology
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">covered technology meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H26FDF0D0340048A8B0417D679E5BF3F1"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  any goods, technology, software, or related material specified in the Missile Technology Control Regime Annex, as in effect on the day before the date of the enactment of this division; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HF49D785BAAFE45559F782A0DE9052EE2"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  any additional goods, technology, software, or related material added to the Missile Technology Control Regime Annex after the day before the date of the enactment of this division.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H31137CE6F4D54071BFCA840B77F5653E"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (7)
               Family member
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">family member meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H1310310A8383438A877CC351E2C738BB"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  a child, grandchild, parent, grandparent, sibling, or spouse; and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H57DD75E118FE44B198A9CFF01A74B097"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  any spouse, widow, or widower of an individual described in subparagraph (A).
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H576D163248094AA3BFEFDC751DCA02CE"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (8)
               Knowingly
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">knowingly has the meaning given that term in section 14 of the Iran Sanctions Act of 1996 (50 U.S.C. 1701 note).
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H5C4F25AA7F73410F9097898A5FE28A49"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (9)
               Missile technology control regime
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Missile Technology Control Regime means the policy statement, between the United States, the United Kingdom, the Federal Republic of Germany, France, Italy, Canada, and Japan, announced on April 16, 1987, to restrict sensitive missile-relevant transfers based on the Missile Technology Control Regime Annex, and any amendments thereto or expansions thereof, as in effect on the day before the date of the enactment of this division.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H2686872CA0C24202B82DB840B9EC40E0"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (10)
               Missile technology control regime annex
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Missile Technology Control Regime Annex means the Guidelines and Equipment and Technology Annex of the Missile Technology Control Regime, and any amendments thereto or updates thereof, as in effect on the day before the date of the enactment of this division.
            
         
      
      
         L
         MAHSA Act 
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H1655BEB09E434DC3BC074EDEE683EA53"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            1.
            SHORT TITLE
            This division may be cited as the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">
                  Mahsa Amini Human rights and Security Accountability Act
                or the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">
                  MAHSA Act
               .
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H8CDA47362E4A49CFA4406A25D27E9615"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            2.
            IMPOSITION OF SANCTIONS ON IRANâ€™S SUPREME LEADERâ€™S OFFICE, ITS APPOINTEES, AND ANY AFFILIATED PERSONS
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HAC3FD436264A42E1A684A06402F67301"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               Findings
               Congress finds the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0C14E5AE6CB7489E925347DB6847540F"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  The Supreme Leader is an institution of the Islamic Republic of Iran.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HE3DAC51777DB4585ABE07E1FA18B8605"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  The Supreme Leader holds ultimate authority over Iranâ€™s judiciary and security apparatus, including the Ministry of Intelligence and Security, law enforcement forces under the Interior Ministry, the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC), and the Basij, a nationwide volunteer paramilitary group subordinate to the IRGC, all of which have engaged in human rights abuses in Iran. Additionally the IRGC, a United States designated Foreign Terrorist Organization, which reports to the Supreme Leader, continues to perpetrate terrorism around the globe, including attempts to kill and kidnap American citizens on United States soil.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HCF145C6C324548079933014203ACCB77"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  The Supreme Leader appoints the head of Iranâ€™s judiciary. International observers continue to criticize the lack of independence of Iranâ€™s judicial system and maintained that trials disregarded international standards of fairness.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H6D0352A4047C4EBD8A5AB0A54C6A6535"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (4)
                  The revolutionary courts, created by Iranâ€™s former Supreme Leader Ruhollah Khomeini, within Iranâ€™s judiciary, are chiefly responsible for hearing cases of political offenses, operate in parallel to Iranâ€™s criminal justice system and routinely hold grossly unfair trials without due process, handing down predetermined verdicts and rubberstamping executions for political purpose.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H7DA0C3E145CF45489CF550A124FFCC23"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (5)
                  The Iranian security and law enforcement forces engage in serious human rights abuse at the behest of the Supreme Leader.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H20613B2ADBA044E6AA17B9AC8CAAB0BC"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (6)
                  Iranâ€™s President, Ebrahim Raisi, sits at the helm of the most sanctioned cabinet in Iranian history which includes internationally sanctioned rights violators. Raisi has supported the recent crackdown on protestors and is a rights violator himself, having served on a <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">death commission in 1988 that led to the execution of several thousand political prisoners in Iran. He most recently served as the head of Iranâ€™s judiciary, a position appointed by Iranâ€™s current Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei, and may likely be a potential candidate to replace Khamenei as Iranâ€™s next Supreme Leader.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H3FB187E9531A429DBB88A95DC3EC73A2"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (7)
                  On September 16, 2022, a 22-year-old woman, Mahsa Amini, died in the detention of the Morality Police after being beaten and detained for allegedly transgressing discriminatory dress codes for women. This tragic incident triggered widespread, pro-womenâ€™s rights, pro-democracy protests across all of Iranâ€™s 31 provinces, calling for the end to Iranâ€™s theocratic regime.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HECF368D18DCF4FDBAC98FF5BFFE43BF8"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (8)
                  In the course of the protests, the Iranian security forcesâ€™ violent crackdown includes mass arrests, well documented beating of protestors, throttling of the internet and telecommunications services, and shooting protestors with live ammunition. Iranian security forces have reportedly killed hundreds of protestors and other civilians, including women and children, and wounded many more.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H924F297962384194866BA46E19FA02AF"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (9)
                  Iranâ€™s Supreme Leader is the leader of the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                             quote-display-start="auto"
                             quote-type="text">Axis of Resistance, which is a network of Tehranâ€™s terror proxy and partner militias materially supported by the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps that targets the United States as well as its allies and partners.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H11381CD68FCB41D89EC3CDB326D658F3"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Sense of congress
               It is the sense of Congress thatâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0A191D2385F14E42AC7DF01769A3379F"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  the United States shall stand with and support the people of Iran in their demand for fundamental human rights;
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0FC600819B9E4B7CA38C01744207287C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  the United States shall continue to hold the Islamic Republic of Iran, particularly the Supreme Leader and President, accountable for abuses of human rights, corruption, and export of terrorism; and
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H31965D7D96204211BA81027BA546A71C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  Iran must immediately end its gross violations of internationally recognized human rights.

         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
