                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  the Committee on Foreign Relations, the Committee on the Judiciary, and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate.
               
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HF5561E33DBFD4C8D8BFA5227DB5DE348"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            6.
            SANCTIONS WITH RESPECT TO THREATS TO CURRENT OR FORMER UNITED STATES OFFICIALS
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H31F4270B8CB545CAB8A07373D7420052"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               On and after the date that is 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the President shall impose the sanctions described in subsection (b) with respect to any foreign person the President determines has, on or after such date of enactment, ordered, directed, or taken material steps to carry out any use of violence or has attempted or threatened to use violence against any current or former official of the Government of the United States.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HA4EC85F1934E4D1688D0567B56844FE1"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Sanctions described
               The sanctions described in this subsection are the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H80EC104FF71B4CA39217063F8900CCA0"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Inadmissibility to united states
                  In the case of a foreign person who is an individualâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H337CCE9C658C43E9809DAB053F58C324"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     ineligibility to receive a visa to enter the United States or to be admitted to the United States; or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HB6BC59BC588E4763A04970599A4EBC11"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     if the individual has been issued a visa or other documentation, revocation, in accordance with section 221(i) of the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1201(i)), of the visa or other documentation.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HA052BE1C53D542ADA1F4402F28FBEC54"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Blocking of property
                  The blocking, in accordance with the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1701 et seq.), of all transactions in all property and interests in property of a foreign person if such property and interests in property are in the United States, come within the United States, or are or come within the possession or control of a United States person.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H43D90B8DF7B44F658A97381198B838E3"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (c)
               Enforcement of blocking of property
               A person that violates, attempts to violate, conspires to violate, or causes a violation of a sanction described in subsection (b)(2) that is imposed by the President or any regulation, license, or order issued to carry out such a sanction shall be subject to the penalties set forth in subsections (b) and (c) of section 206 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1705) to the same extent as a person that commits an unlawful act described in subsection (a) of that section.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H18C70718DC704AD5975FD659FE59C250"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (d)
               Waiver
               The President may waive the application of sanctions under this section for renewable periods not to exceed 180 days if the Presidentâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HA9AA6D13BE9E42B4B9F5AB02CAC29F23"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  determines that such a waiver is in the vital national security interests of the United States; and
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H994F998A1C5D4676AB138BC95069B1F6"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  not less than 15 days before the granting of the waiver, submits to the appropriate congressional committees a notice of and justification for the waiver.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HB8274C3C24ED4C11B4694955CC6FC613"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (e)
               Termination and sunset
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H311115F11F794B398842DDC4919E6FE7"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Termination of sanctions
                  The President may terminate the application of sanctions under this section with respect to a person if the President determines and reports to the appropriate congressional committees not later than 15 days before the termination of the sanctions thatâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H850B1D47F3D6467B9FAA333CE300EAAE"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     credible information exists that the person did not engage in the activity for which sanctions were imposed;
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H4668B29D8C8E49A19F424404243899D9"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     the person has credibly demonstrated a significant change in behavior, has paid an appropriate consequence for the activity for which sanctions were imposed, and has credibly committed to not engage in an activity described in subsection (a) in the future; or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HC06D7EA35582432D84C9B8210D52D525"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (C)
                     the termination of the sanctions is in the vital national security interests of the United States.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H98F52121186D472CA068CE332E3E154E"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Sunset
                  The requirement to impose sanctions under this section shall terminate on the date that is 4 years after the date of the enactment of this division.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H39CF9684F5BF465287E68B0E631715E1"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (f)
               Appropriate congressional committees defined
               In this section, the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">appropriate congressional committees meansâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H24A2225E8CD84CC7A47F43D6AEB4B563"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  the Committee on Foreign Affairs and the Committee on the Judiciary; and
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H2AFF43D50D5040B2A923627244628495"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  the Committee on Foreign Relations and the Committee on the Judiciary.
               
            
         
      
      
         P
         Illicit Captagon Trafficking Suppression Act 
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H67F29B39F027437590AD9DD7394E4607"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            1.
            SHORT TITLE
            This division may be cited as the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">
                  Illicit Captagon Trafficking Suppression Act of 2023
               .
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HE5CDF88129AC49448C27A127D2574951"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            2.
            FINDINGS
            Congress finds the following:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H959CB608D6F44882BBEF2AF0DE4E4B6C"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Industrial scale production of the amphetamine-type stimulant also known as captagon, and the illicit production of precursor chemicals, in territories held by the regime of President Bashar al Assad in Syria are becoming more sophisticated and pose a severe challenge to regional and international security.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HDE89C155A38F4D1FB44D3A3F3380C59F"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Elements of the Government of Syria are key drivers of illicit trafficking in captagon, with ministerial-level complicity in production and smuggling, using other armed groups such as Hizballah for technical and logistical support in captagon production and trafficking.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HA76419751F3040A6B0E7938A8068DBC2"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               As affiliates of the Government of Syria and other actors seek to export captagon, they undermine regional security by empowering a broad range of criminal networks, militant groups, mafia syndicates, and autocratic governments.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HDBE45A2A8F764CA5B0ECD8E91BC82DC0"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            3.
            STATEMENT OF POLICY
            It is the policy of the United States to target individuals, entities, and networks associated with the Government of Syria to dismantle and degrade the transnational criminal organizations, including narcotics trafficking networks, associated with the regime of President Bashar al Assad in Syria and Hizballah.
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HC9EC400D28AD42928F2CF35F6134CC42"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            4.
            IMPOSITION OF SANCTIONS WITH RESPECT TO ILLICIT CAPTAGON TRAFFICKING
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HF84F39C382D24A6C99CF0969E9CAB014"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               The sanctions described in subsection (b) shall be imposed with respect to any foreign person the President determines, on or after the date of enactment of this divisionâ€”
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HAB5C569AAA254260AF7486E83D98E719"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  engages in, or attempts to engage in, activities or transactions that have materially contributed to, or pose a significant risk of materially contributing to, the illicit production and international illicit proliferation of captagon; or
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H9B73EA7EA3E9473D9C15FBAA46B116A8"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  knowingly receives any property or interest in property that the foreign person knowsâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H0312DAB0101A474EA268E9E0F80B2169"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     constitutes or is derived from proceeds of activities or transactions that have materially contributed to, or pose a significant risk of materially contributing to, the illicit production and international illicit proliferation of captagon; or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H4CB5BB19BE684732859DB20C6F37F38B"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     was used or intended to be used to commit or to facilitate activities or transactions that have materially contributed to, or pose a significant risk of materially contributing to, the illicit production and international illicit proliferation of captagon.
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HB33AF33D8BC44B1BACF27C1F8162CF27"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Sanctions described
               The sanctions described in this subsection are the following:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H3908041D77AD4EF2BF44DBEA213F5774"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Blocking of property
                  The President shall exercise all authorities granted under the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1701 et seq.) to the extent necessary to block and prohibit all transactions in property and interests in property of the foreign person if such property and interests in property are in the United States, come within the United States, or come within the possession or control of a United States person.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H6F3BB263B35B45C9BB20B95428ED888C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Ineligibility for visas, admission, or parole
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5B79B9B1D928408A97E6CD05C1B23E75"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     Visas, admission, or parole
                     An alien described in subsection (a) shall beâ€”
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H288933FE38D044A895B467D76287042F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        inadmissible to the United States;
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HE0D871D131E3493FB62BA9ECC0E1AC3F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        ineligible to receive a visa or other documentation to enter the United States; and
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HC1A0EBE2547F4A6A802F259CEDE30756"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (iii)
                        otherwise ineligible to be admitted or paroled into the United States or to receive any other benefit under the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1101 et seq.).
                     
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H51E94250AD364A3F85629A0A0DE3BD9E"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     Current visas revoked
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HCEB3D4D6BFEF47B7A7517D0B2690AB82"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        In general
                        The visa or other entry documentation of any alien described in subsection (a) is subject to revocation regardless of the issue date of the visa or other entry documentation.
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H748E31AB67E247E19BEB05B160AAFD05"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (ii)
                        Immediate effect
                        A revocation under clause (i) shall, in accordance with section 221(i) of the Immigration and Nationality Act (8 U.S.C. 1201(i))â€”
                        <subclause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HCFC68B99C6E34EE8B59F9D033BD9665C"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (I)
                           take effect immediately; and
                        
                        <subclause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HBE88B6738AA84A9A9140790A47305E37"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (II)
                           cancel any other valid visa or entry documentation that is in the possession of the alien.
                        
                     
                  
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HE3E5A4324AC44F79B462590A5BF4FD0B"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (c)
               Penalties
               Any person that violates, or attempts to violate, subsection (b) or any regulation, license, or order issued pursuant to that subsection, shall be subject to the penalties set forth in subsections (b) and (c) of section 206 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1705) to the same extent as a person that commits an unlawful act described in subsection (a) of that section.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H94BD83C4E6694AAA900A9E81D1CB1CD6"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (d)
               Waiver
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H21928B32547045169C213BC23279798C"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  The President may waive the application of sanctions under this section with respect to a foreign person only if, not later than 15 days prior to the date on which the waiver is to take effect, the President submits to the appropriate congressional committees a written determination and justification that the waiver is important to the national security interests of the United States.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5731323FB7474CB68553BBF143303605"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Briefing
                  Not later than 60 days after the issuance of a waiver under paragraph (1), and every 180 days thereafter while the waiver remains in effect, the President shall brief the appropriate congressional committees on the reasons for the waiver.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H3B693154BBAC4CD588C5C6D0C22972A8"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (e)
               Implementation
               The President may exercise all authorities provided under sections 203 and 205 of the International Emergency Economic Powers Act (50 U.S.C. 1702 and 1704) to carry out this section.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H6107E4A2BB3149A48EA80B9B580E0409"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (f)
               Regulations
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H17F1195D26B54C21A558D6403DD5A92F"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  In general
                  The President shall, not later than 120 days after the date of the enactment of this division, promulgate regulations as necessary for the implementation of this section.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5F4D7C58215A4F13B8A5354944DA905E"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Notification to congress
                  Not later than 10 days before the promulgation of regulations under this subsection, the President shall notify the appropriate congressional committees of the proposed regulations and the provisions of this section that the regulations are implementing.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HAC6270CFC1CA4C21820EC1B1D4465011"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (g)
               Exceptions
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H5C3D4F35DA5C43D48CA9657E70789A29"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  Exception for intelligence activities
                  Sanctions under this section shall not apply to any activity subject to the reporting requirements under title V of the National Security Act of 1947 (50 U.S.C. 3091 et seq.) or any authorized intelligence activities of the United States.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HF7823638E83041DF957E84ACF71C672D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  Exception to comply with international obligations and for law enforcement activities
                  Sanctions under this section shall not apply with respect to an alien if admitting or paroling the alien into the United States is necessaryâ€”
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H74F0CEAAC0EB4ABC9263F1AB0E2E7E24"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     to permit the United States to comply with the Agreement regarding the Headquarters of the United Nations, signed at Lake Success June 26, 1947, and entered into force November 21, 1947, between the United Nations and the United States, or other applicable international obligations; or
                  
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H5BF82F4DFA1F483BB8CDBCEE2F74BA44"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (B)
                     to carry out or assist authorized law enforcement activity in the United States.
                  
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="H0ABF61C865594E0A969627AB5CAE3D80"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (3)
                  Humanitarian assistance
                  <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H02604A525D914E31A6B0C1949D33EF66"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (A)
                     In general
                     Sanctions under this division shall not apply toâ€”
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="HD204336E9B8C4D5B8F4DADE252DF0381"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (i)
                        the conduct or facilitation of a transaction for the provision of agricultural commodities, food, medicine, medical devices, humanitarian assistance, or for humanitarian purposes; or
                     
                     <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"

                              qb-display-quote="yes">

            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H15DC574DABE148EB84BFAC825AC9A12D"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Captagon
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">captagon means any compound, mixture, or preparation which contains any quantity of a stimulant in schedule I or II of section 202 of the Controlled Substances Act (21 U.S.C. 812), includingâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H55A0B2E425234BF5BB169F6F96306AF4"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">

               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H8C9CC334C254448CB5E9750E5B6B5EB8"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  any immediate precursor or controlled substance analogue of such a stimulant, as defined in section 102 of the Controlled Substances Act (21 U.S.C. 802); and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H5E4EC6858F9B4C40B621F1D42EE93329"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  any isomers, esters, ethers, salts, and salts of isomers, esters, and ethers of such a stimulant, whenever the existence of such isomers, esters, ethers, and salts is possible within the specific chemical designation.

                        id="HA10086C906BF4E8C8ADA63994EB76BCB"

               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"

                              qb-display-quote="yes">

         Q
         End Financing for Hamas and State Sponsors of Terrorism Act 
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HC199455E8C0A4616BE842FB2B08F0477"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            1.
            SHORT TITLE
            This division may be cited as the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">End Financing for Hamas and State Sponsors of Terrorism Act.
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HAB3BACFE870B4D0CB32D55925435E0FB"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            2.
            REPORT ON FINANCING FOR HAMAS
            Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this division, the Secretary of the Treasury shall submit to the Committee on Foreign Affairs and the Committee on Financial Services of the House of Representatives and to the Committee on Foreign Relations and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate a report (which shall be in unclassified form but may include a classified annex) that includesâ€”
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H4E8206BF9E864E98A6FA2D5BFBE54C94"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               an analysis of the major sources of financing to Hamas;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H5BFF09A0A35047A09D06771A00B1904F"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               a description of United States and multilateral efforts to disrupt illicit financial flows involving Hamas;
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H0CA6AB67B9174E9797BBA40D8DDE89AD"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               an evaluation of United States efforts to undermine the ability of Hamas to finance armed hostilities against Israel; and
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HDEA11811409E4E47BFF9E16BA19EDC86"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               an implementation plan with respect to the multilateral strategy described in section 3.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H384D17FA67D84C15AC0CA42FFC9E4655"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            3.
            MULTILATERAL STRATEGY TO DISRUPT HAMAS FINANCING
            The Secretary of the Treasury, through participation in the G7, and other appropriate fora, shall develop a strategy in coordination with United States allies and partners to ensure that Hamas is incapable of financing armed hostilities against Israel.
         
      
      
         R
         Holding Iranian Leaders Accountable Act 
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H74F88975532F4848B41130FD68D1DDFB"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            1.
            SHORT TITLE
            This division may be cited as the <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                       quote-display-start="auto"
                       quote-type="text">
                  Holding Iranian Leaders Accountable Act of 2024
               .
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H22CBDCBFC97C4BFFBAF5DA4E6349404A"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            2.
            FINDINGS
            The Congress finds the following:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H57787F0F7346496EB2228FCA2CE989DF"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Iran is characterized by high levels of official and institutional corruption, and substantial involvement by Iranâ€™s security forces, particularly the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps (IRGC), in the economy.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HFB7E60D6E88540208AE64F560B82A087"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               The Department of Treasury in 2019 designated the Islamic Republic of Iranâ€™s financial sector as a jurisdiction of primary money laundering concern, concluding, <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Iran has developed covert methods for accessing the international financial system and pursuing its malign activities, including misusing banks and exchange houses, operating procurement networks that utilize front or shell companies, exploiting commercial shipping, and masking illicit transactions using senior officials, including those at the Central Bank of Iran (CBI)..
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HE41FE2C7526E492CB86B51B047498EAA"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               In June 2019, the Financial Action Task Force (FATF) urged all jurisdictions to require increased supervisory examination for branches and subsidiaries of financial institutions based in Iran. The FATF later called upon its members to introduce enhanced relevant reporting mechanisms or systematic reporting of financial transactions, and require increased external audit requirements, for financial groups with respect to any of their branches and subsidiaries located in Iran.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H2AB47AC5BA3343068A1E1AACA1FF4BAA"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               According to the State Departmentâ€™s <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Country Reports on Terrorism in 2021, <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Iran continued to be the leading state sponsor of terrorism, facilitating a wide range of terrorist and other illicit activities around the world. Regionally, Iran supported acts of terrorism in Bahrain, Iraq, Lebanon, Syria, and Yemen through proxies and partner groups such as Hizballah and Hamas..
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HF9C431737B3B476CBB6B8B8D5D82B358"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">

         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H50EE344793CA4785B20F10BAF4B8EAAE"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            4.
            RESTRICTIONS ON CERTAIN FINANCIAL INSTITUTIONS
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H0585CF3AD38245338685BAF1C1F3AE38"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               In general
               Not later than the date that is 90 days after submitting a report described under section 3(a)(1), the Secretary shall undertake the following with respect to a financial institution that is described under section 3(a)(1)(C) and listed in the report:
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HEF59099C9F0C4F1284802FEA9464960D"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (1)
                  If the financial institution is a United States financial institution, require the closure of any account described in section 3(a)(1)(C)(i), and prohibit the provision of significant financial services, directly or indirectly, to a natural person covered by the report.
               
               <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                           id="HB60D76CABA694EE6897DB63BD36A4CD7"
                           qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (2)
                  If the financial institution is a foreign financial institution, actively seek the closure of any account described in section 3(a)(1)(C)(i), and the cessation of significant financial services to a natural person covered by the report, using any existing authorities of the Secretary, as appropriate.
               
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="HA8EBB488681B40D6875921A49D79CE44"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Suspension
               The Secretary may suspend the application of subsection (a) with respect to a financial institution upon reporting to the appropriate Members of Congress that the suspension is in the national interest of the United States, with a detailed explanation of the reasons therefor.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="HB295641B0E83435AB43F3B9F71F1C0A6"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            5.
            EXCEPTIONS FOR NATIONAL SECURITY; IMPLEMENTATION AUTHORITY
            The following activities shall be exempt from requirements under sections 3 and 4:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H4550840EE2B44744B46A33EF29492F82"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Any activity subject to the reporting requirements under title V of the National Security Act of 1947 (50 U.S.C. 3091 et seq.), or to any authorized intelligence activities of the United States.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HD98F019E447847B0B3824443DDA6F6F2"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               The admission of an alien to the United States if such admission is necessary to comply with United States obligations under the Agreement between the United Nations and the United States of America regarding the Headquarters of the United Nations, signed at Lake Success June 26, 1947, and entered into force November 21, 1947, or under the Convention on Consular Relations, done at Vienna April 24, 1963, and entered into force March 19, 1967, or other applicable international obligations of the United States.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HC9CF8AE6DEF64C19AB20EBDC5A4859F7"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               The conduct or facilitation of a transaction for the sale of agricultural commodities, food, medicine, or medical devices to Iran or for the provision of humanitarian assistance to the people of Iran, including engaging in a financial transaction relating to humanitarian assistance or for humanitarian purposes or transporting goods or services that are necessary to carry out operations relating to humanitarian assistance or humanitarian purposes.
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H788D585C4CA7454CA8766EE6B4036F59"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            6.
            SUNSET
            The provisions of this division shall have no force or effect on the earlier ofâ€”
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H38801D51F8674F91A2414C7D24180E04"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               the date that is 5 years after the date of enactment of this division; or
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H4C0B0C2144624CCF8FDAD5CE54AB42BB"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               30 days after the Secretary reports in writing to the appropriate Members of Congress thatâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H598909C20E834DB0B5924681B8CEB93C"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  Iran is not a jurisdiction of primary money laundering concern; or
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H56988FA9C41348FDAE25A426475470FC"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  the Government of Iran is providing significant cooperation to the United States for the purpose of preventing acts of international terrorism, or for the promotion of any other strategic objective that is important to the national interest of the United States, as specified in the report by the Secretary.
               
            
         
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"
                   id="H0714BA677F0D4D03A2C1CEB257E18F7B"
                   qb-display-quote="yes"
                   section-type="subsequent-section">
            7.
            DEFINITIONS
            For purposes of this division:
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H21534E108E714C8594C568315DA2F883"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               Appropriate members of congress
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">appropriate Members of Congress means the Speaker and Minority Leader of the House of Representatives, the Majority Leader and Minority Leader of the Senate, the Chairman and Ranking Member of the Committee on Foreign Affairs and the Committee on Financial Services of the House of Representatives, and the Chairman and Ranking Member of the Committee on Foreign Relations and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H2A835604C1C248DA8433E30BC99EEC09"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               Financial institution
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">financial institution means a United States financial institution or a foreign financial institution.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HBE10F8482BFE485889D2E1F1A1B665EE"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (3)
               Foreign financial institution
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">foreign financial institution has the meaning given that term in section 561.308 of title 31, Code of Federal Regulations.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H497DF84C585942BFB6E98303334C6EAD"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (4)
               Funds
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">funds meansâ€”
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H344A8B80393B4671B8233C0F4BD02F9E"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (A)
                  cash;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H00E3468ED3264B0F949B24FCAEF7E54F"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (B)
                  equity;
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H49002C8BBFC94D11B0529123A339D77E"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (C)
                  any other asset whose value is derived from a contractual claim, including bank deposits, bonds, stocks, a security as defined in section 2(a) of the Securities Act of 1933 (15 U.S.C. 77b(a)), or a security or an equity security as defined in section 3(a) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 (15 U.S.C. 78c(a)); and
               
               <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H12F0AA25EC944C3F8D4267CEFC5B76CF"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                  (D)
                  anything else that the Secretary determines appropriate.
               
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HA48C1371E59E4456A40F3D0D62E02C40"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (5)
               Knowingly
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">knowingly with respect to conduct, a circumstance, or a result, means that a person has actual knowledge, or should have known, of the conduct, the circumstance, or the result.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HAEBACC57E85742BAB21D4931D18ABB60"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (6)
               Secretary
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">Secretary means the Secretary of the Treasury.
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="HDC3958B86ACE4AC8879395AF45F7E679"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (7)
               United states financial institution
               The term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">United States financial institution has the meaning given the term <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                          quote-display-start="auto"
                          quote-type="text">U.S. financial institution under section 561.309 of title 31, Code of Federal Regulations.

            2.
            SANCTIONS ON FOREIGN FINANCIAL INSTITUTIONS WITH RESPECT TO THE PURCHASE OF PETROLEUM PRODUCTS AND UNMANNED AERIAL VEHICLES FROM IRAN
            Section 1245(d) of the National Defense Authorization Act for Fiscal Year 2012 (22 U.S.C. 8513a(d)) is amendedâ€”
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H6E42EDAD69FF4281A50E82888EC3C21E"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (1)
               by redesignating paragraph (5) as paragraph (6); and
            
            <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                        id="H78B30E93D9164435ADDD4ED41D7D4A0D"
                        qb-display-quote="yes">
               (2)
               by inserting after paragraph (4) the following new paragraph:
               <quoted-block display-end-quotes="yes"
                              display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              display-quotes="yes"
                              id="HBDF7FAD45C934B6880E2CE95C2C1454D"
                              style="OLC">
                  <paragraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                              id="H595B431709D640DBA8C8CB3F2198EFEE"
                              qb-display-quote="yes">
                     (5)
                     Applicability of sanctions with respect to chinese financial institutions
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HC315B0D085754E4EA85619BBD9A5B300"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (A)
                        In general
                        For the purpose of paragraph (1)(A), a <quote quote-display-end="auto"
                                   quote-display-start="auto"
                                   quote-type="text">significant financial transaction shall include, based on relevant facts and circumstances, any transactionâ€”
                        <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HAEF6221F393E49B686B844DCFCCADBF9"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (i)
                           by a Chinese financial institution (without regard to the size, number, frequency, or nature of the transaction) involving the purchase of petroleum or petroleum products from Iran; and
                        
                        <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="H85CA84D244864CC29776BC126D57B630"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (ii)
                           by a foreign financial institution (without regard to the size, number, frequency, or nature of the transaction) involving the purchase of Iranian unmanned aerial vehicles (UAVs), UAV parts, or related systems.
                        
                     
                     <subparagraph display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                    id="HE537A7F212014C12BA0F89F9DDD6936E"
                                    qb-display-quote="yes">
                        (B)
                        Determination required
                        Not later than 180 days after the date of the enactment of this paragraph and every year thereafter for 5 years, the President shallâ€”
                        <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HFF88E65AA19E45F4A9EB2DEA207165F1"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (i)
                           determine whether anyâ€”
                           <subclause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H8C58CE9F71264E22807ABCA94BD6D1D0"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                              (I)
                              Chinese financial institution has engaged in a significant financial transaction as described in paragraph (1)(A)(i); and
                           
                           <subclause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                       id="H0657D909AC164C5B9EC437515B8FBBBF"
                                       qb-display-quote="yes">
                              (II)
                              financial institution has engaged in a significant financial transaction as described in paragraph (1)(A)(ii); and
                           
                        
                        <clause display-inline="no-display-inline"
                                 id="HCC9E97ABB38D45609AA57457264E83FF"
                                 qb-display-quote="yes">
                           (ii)
                           transmit the determination under clause (i) to the Committee on Foreign Affairs and the Committee on Financial Services of the House of Representatives and to the Committee on Foreign Relations and the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs of the Senate.

         T
         Budgetary Effects
         <section display-inline="no-display-inline"

            1.
            BUDGETARY EFFECTS
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H184948A69AA84DD68EBA0D4B7D5FC995"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (a)
               Statutory PAYGO scorecards
               The budgetary effects of division D and each subsequent division of this Act shall not be entered on either PAYGO scorecard maintained pursuant to section 4(d) of the Statutory Pay-As-You-Go Act of 2010.
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
                         id="H4C19FD6C37A944E18491F4373A706C36"
                         qb-display-quote="yes">
               (b)
               Senate PAYGO scorecards
               The budgetary effects of division D and each subsequent division of this Act shall not be entered on any PAYGO scorecard maintained for purposes of section 4106 of H. Con. Res. 71 (115th Congress).
            
            <subsection display-inline="no-display-inline"
